Text: Give raises, hire staff that have commensurate skills for the job, pay people what their skills are worth in the competitive market.  

The State Auditor should do a salary evaluation for all State Universities and make the salaries and wages consistent.  NMT employees are paid 20%-25% lower than their counterparts at UNM and NMSU.

Housing in Socorro is sub par in many cases and controlled by a small group of people who conspire to set rent prices for their tenants according to their salaries which are made public.  The University should consider that rental housing is both expensive and limited when determining employment offers; or, alternatively, work with local realtors to assist in setting fair prices for students and employees.

Public utilities in Socorro are extremely expensive with no visibility as to how rates are determined.  As NMT is the largest customer in the city, it has the ability to question the rates and ample staff to pursue answers to questions on rates. 

Many NMT employees attain high levels of management with high salary levels due to seniority or nepotism and do not have the requisite skills or education for their positions.  This is a high risk for the university and prevents qualified people from accessing these positions in the long term.
